   212	        &self,
   213	        projection: &ProjectionExec,
   214	    ) -> Result<Option<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>>> {
   215	        // If the projection does not narrow the schema, we should not try to push it down:
   216	        let proj_exprs = projection.expr();
   217	        if proj_exprs.len() >= projection.input().schema().fields().len() {
   218	            return Ok(None);
   219	        }

   226	                let Some(updated_lex) = update_ordering_requirement(lex, proj_exprs)?
   227	                else {
   228	                    return Ok(None);
   229	                };

   231	            }

    fn fmt_as(
        &self,
        t: DisplayFormatType,

    ) -> std::fmt::Result {

            // The default / verbose formats are used by EXPLAIN output and
            // should include the requirements tracked by this helper node.

                write!(

    18	//! The GlobalOrderRequire optimizer rule either:
    19	//! - Adds an auxiliary `OutputRequirementExec` operator to keep track of global
    20	//!   ordering and distribution requirement across rules, or
    21	//! - Removes the auxiliary `OutputRequirementExec` operator from the physical plan.
    22	//!   Since the `OutputRequirementExec` operator is only a helper operator, it
    23	//!   shouldn't occur in the final plan (i.e. the executed plan).
    24	
    25	use std::sync::Arc;
    26	
    27	use crate::PhysicalOptimizerRule;
    28	
    29	use datafusion_common::config::ConfigOptions;
    30	use datafusion_common::tree_node::{Transformed, TransformedResult, TreeNode};
    31	use datafusion_common::{Result, Statistics};
    32	use datafusion_execution::TaskContext;
    33	use datafusion_physical_expr::Distribution;
    34	use datafusion_physical_expr_common::sort_expr::OrderingRequirements;
    35	use datafusion_physical_plan::projection::{
    36	    make_with_child, update_expr, update_ordering_requirement, ProjectionExec,
    37	};
    38	use datafusion_physical_plan::sorts::sort::SortExec;
    39	use datafusion_physical_plan::sorts::sort_preserving_merge::SortPreservingMergeExec;

    41	    DisplayAs, DisplayFormatType, ExecutionPlan, ExecutionPlanProperties, PlanProperties,
    42	    SendableRecordBatchStream,

    45	/// This rule either adds or removes [`OutputRequirements`]s to/from the physical
    46	/// plan according to its `mode` attribute, which is set by the constructors
    47	/// `new_add_mode` and `new_remove_mode`. With this rule, we can keep track of
    48	/// the global requirements (ordering and distribution) across rules.
    49	///
    50	/// The primary use case of this node and rule is to specify and preserve the desired output
    51	/// ordering and distribution the entire plan. When sending to a single client, a single partition may
    52	/// be desirable, but when sending to a multi-partitioned writer, keeping multiple partitions may be
    53	/// better.
    54	#[derive(Debug)]
    55	pub struct OutputRequirements {
    56	    mode: RuleMode,
    57	}
    58	
    59	impl OutputRequirements {
    60	    /// Create a new rule which works in `Add` mode; i.e. it simply adds a
    61	    /// top-level [`OutputRequirementExec`] into the physical plan to keep track
    62	    /// of global ordering and distribution requirements if there are any.
    63	    /// Note that this rule should run at the beginning.
    64	    pub fn new_add_mode() -> Self {
    65	        Self {
    66	            mode: RuleMode::Add,
    67	        }
    68	    }
    69	
    70	    /// Create a new rule which works in `Remove` mode; i.e. it simply removes
    71	    /// the top-level [`OutputRequirementExec`] from the physical plan if there is
    72	    /// any. We do this because a `OutputRequirementExec` is an ancillary,
    73	    /// non-executable operator whose sole purpose is to track global
    74	    /// requirements during optimization. Therefore, a
    75	    /// `OutputRequirementExec` should not appear in the final plan.
    76	    pub fn new_remove_mode() -> Self {
    77	        Self {
    78	            mode: RuleMode::Remove,
    79	        }
    80	    }
    81	}
    82	
    83	#[derive(Debug, Ord, PartialOrd, PartialEq, Eq, Hash)]
    84	enum RuleMode {
    85	    Add,
    86	    Remove,
    87	}
    88	
    89	/// An ancillary, non-executable operator whose sole purpose is to track global
    90	/// requirements during optimization. It imposes
    91	/// - the ordering requirement in its `order_requirement` attribute.
    92	/// - the distribution requirement in its `dist_requirement` attribute.
    93	///
    94	/// See [`OutputRequirements`] for more details
    95	#[derive(Debug)]
    96	pub struct OutputRequirementExec {
    97	    input: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
    98	    order_requirement: Option<OrderingRequirements>,
    99	    dist_requirement: Distribution,
   100	    cache: PlanProperties,
   101	}
   102	
   103	impl OutputRequirementExec {
   104	    pub fn new(
   105	        input: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   106	        requirements: Option<OrderingRequirements>,
   107	        dist_requirement: Distribution,
   108	    ) -> Self {
   109	        let cache = Self::compute_properties(&input);
   110	        Self {
   111	            input,
   112	            order_requirement: requirements,
   113	            dist_requirement,
   114	            cache,
   115	        }
   116	    }
   117	
   118	    pub fn input(&self) -> Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan> {
   119	        Arc::clone(&self.input)
   120	    }
   121	
   122	    /// This function creates the cache object that stores the plan properties such as schema, equivalence properties, ordering, partitioning, etc.
   123	    fn compute_properties(input: &Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>) -> PlanProperties {
   124	        PlanProperties::new(
   125	            input.equivalence_properties().clone(), // Equivalence Properties
   126	            input.output_partitioning().clone(),    // Output Partitioning
   127	            input.pipeline_behavior(),              // Pipeline Behavior
   128	            input.boundedness(),                    // Boundedness
   129	        )
   130	    }
   131	}
   132	
   133	impl DisplayAs for OutputRequirementExec {
   134	    fn fmt_as(
   135	        &self,
   136	        t: DisplayFormatType,
   137	        f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter,
   138	    ) -> std::fmt::Result {
   139	        match t {
   140	            DisplayFormatType::Default | DisplayFormatType::Verbose => {
   141	                write!(f, "OutputRequirementExec")
   142	            }
   143	            DisplayFormatType::TreeRender => {
   144	                // TODO: collect info
   145	                write!(f, "")
   146	            }
   147	        }
   148	    }
   149	}

   151	impl ExecutionPlan for OutputRequirementExec {
   152	    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {
   153	        "OutputRequirementExec"
   154	    }
   155	
   156	    fn as_any(&self) -> &dyn std::any::Any {
   157	        self
   158	    }
   159	
   160	    fn properties(&self) -> &PlanProperties {
   161	        &self.cache
   162	    }
   163	
   164	    fn benefits_from_input_partitioning(&self) -> Vec<bool> {
   165	        vec![false]
   166	    }
   167	
   168	    fn required_input_distribution(&self) -> Vec<Distribution> {
   169	        vec![self.dist_requirement.clone()]
   170	    }
   171	
   172	    fn maintains_input_order(&self) -> Vec<bool> {
   173	        vec![true]
   174	    }
   175	
   176	    fn children(&self) -> Vec<&Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   177	        vec![&self.input]
   178	    }
   179	
   180	    fn required_input_ordering(&self) -> Vec<Option<OrderingRequirements>> {
   181	        vec![self.order_requirement.clone()]
   182	    }
   183	
   184	    fn with_new_children(
   185	        self: Arc<Self>,
   186	        mut children: Vec<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>>,
   187	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   188	        Ok(Arc::new(Self::new(
   189	            children.remove(0), // has a single child
   190	            self.order_requirement.clone(),
   191	            self.dist_requirement.clone(),
   192	        )))
   193	    }
   194	
   195	    fn execute(
   196	        &self,
   197	        _partition: usize,
   198	        _context: Arc<TaskContext>,
   199	    ) -> Result<SendableRecordBatchStream> {
   200	        unreachable!();
   201	    }
   202	
   203	    fn statistics(&self) -> Result<Statistics> {
   204	        self.input.partition_statistics(None)
   205	    }
   206	
   207	    fn partition_statistics(&self, partition: Option<usize>) -> Result<Statistics> {
   208	        self.input.partition_statistics(partition)
   209	    }
   210	
   211	    fn try_swapping_with_projection(
   212	        &self,
   213	        projection: &ProjectionExec,
   214	    ) -> Result<Option<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>>> {
   215	        // If the projection does not narrow the schema, we should not try to push it down:
   216	        let proj_exprs = projection.expr();
   217	        if proj_exprs.len() >= projection.input().schema().fields().len() {
   218	            return Ok(None);
   219	        }
   220	
   221	        let mut requirements = self.required_input_ordering().swap_remove(0);
   222	        if let Some(reqs) = requirements {
   223	            let mut updated_reqs = vec![];
   224	            let (lexes, soft) = reqs.into_alternatives();
   225	            for lex in lexes.into_iter() {
   226	                let Some(updated_lex) = update_ordering_requirement(lex, proj_exprs)?
   227	                else {
   228	                    return Ok(None);
   229	                };
   230	                updated_reqs.push(updated_lex);
   231	            }
   232	            requirements = OrderingRequirements::new_alternatives(updated_reqs, soft);
   233	        }
   234	
   235	        let dist_req = match &self.required_input_distribution()[0] {
   236	            Distribution::HashPartitioned(exprs) => {
   237	                let mut updated_exprs = vec![];
   238	                for expr in exprs {
   239	                    let Some(new_expr) = update_expr(expr, projection.expr(), false)?
   240	                    else {
   241	                        return Ok(None);
   242	                    };
   243	                    updated_exprs.push(new_expr);
   244	                }
   245	                Distribution::HashPartitioned(updated_exprs)
   246	            }
   247	            dist => dist.clone(),
   248	        };
   249	
   250	        make_with_child(projection, &self.input()).map(|input| {
   251	            let e = OutputRequirementExec::new(input, requirements, dist_req);
   252	            Some(Arc::new(e) as _)
   253	        })
   254	    }
   255	}
   256	
   257	impl PhysicalOptimizerRule for OutputRequirements {
   258	    fn optimize(
   259	        &self,
   260	        plan: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   261	        _config: &ConfigOptions,
   262	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   263	        match self.mode {
   264	            RuleMode::Add => require_top_ordering(plan),
   265	            RuleMode::Remove => plan
   266	                .transform_up(|plan| {
   267	                    if let Some(sort_req) =
   268	                        plan.as_any().downcast_ref::<OutputRequirementExec>()
   269	                    {
   270	                        Ok(Transformed::yes(sort_req.input()))
   271	                    } else {
   272	                        Ok(Transformed::no(plan))
   273	                    }
   274	                })
   275	                .data(),
   276	        }
   277	    }
   278	
   279	    fn name(&self) -> &str {
   280	        "OutputRequirements"
   281	    }
   282	
   283	    fn schema_check(&self) -> bool {
   284	        true
   285	    }
   286	}
   287	
   288	/// This functions adds ancillary `OutputRequirementExec` to the physical plan, so that
   289	/// global requirements are not lost during optimization.
   290	fn require_top_ordering(plan: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   291	    let (new_plan, is_changed) = require_top_ordering_helper(plan)?;
   292	    if is_changed {
   293	        Ok(new_plan)
   294	    } else {
   295	        // Add `OutputRequirementExec` to the top, with no specified ordering and distribution requirement.
   296	        Ok(Arc::new(OutputRequirementExec::new(
   297	            new_plan,
   298	            // there is no ordering requirement
   299	            None,
   300	            Distribution::UnspecifiedDistribution,
   301	        )) as _)
   302	    }
   303	}
   304	
   305	/// Helper function that adds an ancillary `OutputRequirementExec` to the given plan.
   306	/// First entry in the tuple is resulting plan, second entry indicates whether any
   307	/// `OutputRequirementExec` is added to the plan.
   308	fn require_top_ordering_helper(
   309	    plan: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   310	) -> Result<(Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>, bool)> {
   311	    let mut children = plan.children();
   312	    // Global ordering defines desired ordering in the final result.
   313	    if children.len() != 1 {
   314	        Ok((plan, false))
   315	    } else if let Some(sort_exec) = plan.as_any().downcast_ref::<SortExec>() {
   316	        // In case of constant columns, output ordering of the `SortExec` would
   317	        // be an empty set. Therefore; we check the sort expression field to
   318	        // assign the requirements.
   319	        let req_ordering = sort_exec.expr();
   320	        let req_dist = sort_exec.required_input_distribution().swap_remove(0);
   321	        let reqs = OrderingRequirements::from(req_ordering.clone());
   322	        Ok((
   323	            Arc::new(OutputRequirementExec::new(plan, Some(reqs), req_dist)) as _,
   324	            true,
   325	        ))
   326	    } else if let Some(spm) = plan.as_any().downcast_ref::<SortPreservingMergeExec>() {
   327	        let reqs = OrderingRequirements::from(spm.expr().clone());
   328	        Ok((
   329	            Arc::new(OutputRequirementExec::new(
   330	                plan,
   331	                Some(reqs),
   332	                Distribution::SinglePartition,
   333	            )) as _,
   334	            true,
   335	        ))
   336	    } else if plan.maintains_input_order()[0]
   337	        && (plan.required_input_ordering()[0]
   338	            .as_ref()
   339	            .is_none_or(|o| matches!(o, OrderingRequirements::Soft(_))))
   340	    {
   341	        // Keep searching for a `SortExec` as long as ordering is maintained,
   342	        // and on-the-way operators do not themselves require an ordering.
   343	        // When an operator requires an ordering, any `SortExec` below can not
   344	        // be responsible for (i.e. the originator of) the global ordering.
   345	        let (new_child, is_changed) =
   346	            require_top_ordering_helper(Arc::clone(children.swap_remove(0)))?;
   347	        Ok((plan.with_new_children(vec![new_child])?, is_changed))
   348	    } else {
   349	        // Stop searching, there is no global ordering desired for the query.
   350	        Ok((plan, false))
   351	    }
   352	}
   353

   355

   210	
   211	    fn try_swapping_with_projection(
   212	        &self,
   213	        projection: &ProjectionExec,
   214	    ) -> Result<Option<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>>> {
   215	        // If the projection does not narrow the schema, we should not try to push it down:
   216	        let proj_exprs = projection.expr();
   217	        if proj_exprs.len() >= projection.input().schema().fields().len() {
   218	            return Ok(None);
   219	        }
   220	
   221	        let mut requirements = self.required_input_ordering().swap_remove(0);
   222	        if let Some(reqs) = requirements {
   223	            let mut updated_reqs = vec![];
   224	            let (lexes, soft) = reqs.into_alternatives();
   225	            for lex in lexes.into_iter() {
   226	                let Some(updated_lex) = update_ordering_requirement(lex, proj_exprs)?
   227	                else {
   228	                    return Ok(None);
   229	                };
   230	                updated_reqs.push(updated_lex);
   231	            }
   232	            requirements = OrderingRequirements::new_alternatives(updated_reqs, soft);
   233	        }
   234	
   235	        let dist_req = match &self.required_input_distribution()[0] {
   236	            Distribution::HashPartitioned(exprs) => {
   237	                let mut updated_exprs = vec![];
   238	                for expr in exprs {
   239	                    let Some(new_expr) = update_expr(expr, projection.expr(), false)?
   240	                    else {
   241	                        return Ok(None);
   242	                    };
   243	                    updated_exprs.push(new_expr);
   244	                }
   245	                Distribution::HashPartitioned(updated_exprs)
   246	            }
   247	            dist => dist.clone(),
   248	        };
   249	
   250	        make_with_child(projection, &self.input()).map(|input| {
   251	            let e = OutputRequirementExec::new(input, requirements, dist_req);
   252	            Some(Arc::new(e) as _)
   253	        })
   254	    }
   255	}

    18	//! The GlobalOrderRequire optimizer rule either:
    19	//! - Adds an auxiliary `OutputRequirementExec` operator to keep track of global
    20	//!   ordering and distribution requirement across rules, or
    21	//! - Removes the auxiliary `OutputRequirementExec` operator from the physical plan.
    22	//!   Since the `OutputRequirementExec` operator is only a helper operator, it
    23	//!   shouldn't occur in the final plan (i.e. the executed plan).
    24	
    25	use std::sync::Arc;
    26	
    27	use crate::PhysicalOptimizerRule;
    28	
    29	use datafusion_common::config::ConfigOptions;
    30	use datafusion_common::tree_node::{Transformed, TransformedResult, TreeNode};
    31	use datafusion_common::{Result, Statistics};
    32	use datafusion_execution::TaskContext;
    33	use datafusion_physical_expr::Distribution;
    34	use datafusion_physical_expr_common::sort_expr::OrderingRequirements;
    35	use datafusion_physical_plan::projection::{
    36	    make_with_child, update_expr, update_ordering_requirement, ProjectionExec,
    37	};
    38	use datafusion_physical_plan::sorts::sort::SortExec;
    39	use datafusion_physical_plan::sorts::sort_preserving_merge::SortPreservingMergeExec;
    40	use datafusion_physical_plan::{
    41	    DisplayAs, DisplayFormatType, ExecutionPlan, ExecutionPlanProperties, PlanProperties,
    42	    SendableRecordBatchStream,
    43	};
    44	
    45	/// This rule either adds or removes [`OutputRequirements`]s to/from the physical
    46	/// plan according to its `mode` attribute, which is set by the constructors
    47	/// `new_add_mode` and `new_remove_mode`. With this rule, we can keep track of
    48	/// the global requirements (ordering and distribution) across rules.
    49	///
    50	/// The primary use case of this node and rule is to specify and preserve the desired output
    51	/// ordering and distribution the entire plan. When sending to a single client, a single partition may
    52	/// be desirable, but when sending to a multi-partitioned writer, keeping multiple partitions may be
    53	/// better.
    54	#[derive(Debug)]
    55	pub struct OutputRequirements {
    56	    mode: RuleMode,
    57	}
    58	
    59	impl OutputRequirements {
    60	    /// Create a new rule which works in `Add` mode; i.e. it simply adds a
    61	    /// top-level [`OutputRequirementExec`] into the physical plan to keep track
    62	    /// of global ordering and distribution requirements if there are any.
    63	    /// Note that this rule should run at the beginning.
    64	    pub fn new_add_mode() -> Self {
    65	        Self {
    66	            mode: RuleMode::Add,
    67	        }
    68	    }
    69	
    70	    /// Create a new rule which works in `Remove` mode; i.e. it simply removes
    71	    /// the top-level [`OutputRequirementExec`] from the physical plan if there is
    72	    /// any. We do this because a `OutputRequirementExec` is an ancillary,
    73	    /// non-executable operator whose sole purpose is to track global
    74	    /// requirements during optimization. Therefore, a
    75	    /// `OutputRequirementExec` should not appear in the final plan.
    76	    pub fn new_remove_mode() -> Self {
    77	        Self {
    78	            mode: RuleMode::Remove,
    79	        }
    80	    }
    81	}
    82	
    83	#[derive(Debug, Ord, PartialOrd, PartialEq, Eq, Hash)]
    84	enum RuleMode {
    85	    Add,
    86	    Remove,
    87	}
    88	
    89	/// An ancillary, non-executable operator whose sole purpose is to track global
    90	/// requirements during optimization. It imposes
    91	/// - the ordering requirement in its `order_requirement` attribute.
    92	/// - the distribution requirement in its `dist_requirement` attribute.
    93	///
    94	/// See [`OutputRequirements`] for more details
    95	#[derive(Debug)]
    96	pub struct OutputRequirementExec {
    97	    input: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
    98	    order_requirement: Option<OrderingRequirements>,
    99	    dist_requirement: Distribution,
   100	    cache: PlanProperties,
   101	}
   102	
   103	impl OutputRequirementExec {
   104	    pub fn new(
   105	        input: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   106	        requirements: Option<OrderingRequirements>,
   107	        dist_requirement: Distribution,
   108	    ) -> Self {
   109	        let cache = Self::compute_properties(&input);
   110	        Self {
   111	            input,
   112	            order_requirement: requirements,
   113	            dist_requirement,
   114	            cache,
   115	        }
   116	    }
   117	
   118	    pub fn input(&self) -> Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan> {
   119	        Arc::clone(&self.input)
   120	    }
   121	
   122	    /// This function creates the cache object that stores the plan properties such as schema, equivalence properties, ordering, partitioning, etc.
   123	    fn compute_properties(input: &Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>) -> PlanProperties {
   124	        PlanProperties::new(
   125	            input.equivalence_properties().clone(), // Equivalence Properties
   126	            input.output_partitioning().clone(),    // Output Partitioning
   127	            input.pipeline_behavior(),              // Pipeline Behavior
   128	            input.boundedness(),                    // Boundedness
   129	        )
   130	    }
   131	}
   132	
   133	impl DisplayAs for OutputRequirementExec {
   134	    fn fmt_as(
   135	        &self,
   136	        t: DisplayFormatType,
   137	        f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter,
   138	    ) -> std::fmt::Result {
   139	        match t {
   140	            DisplayFormatType::Default | DisplayFormatType::Verbose => {
   141	                write!(f, "OutputRequirementExec")
   142	            }
   143	            DisplayFormatType::TreeRender => {
   144	                // TODO: collect info
   145	                write!(f, "")
   146	            }
   147	        }
   148	    }
   149	}
   150	
   151	impl ExecutionPlan for OutputRequirementExec {
   152	    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {
   153	        "OutputRequirementExec"
   154	    }
   155	
   156	    fn as_any(&self) -> &dyn std::any::Any {
   157	        self
   158	    }
   159	
   160	    fn properties(&self) -> &PlanProperties {
   161	        &self.cache
   162	    }
   163	
   164	    fn benefits_from_input_partitioning(&self) -> Vec<bool> {
   165	        vec![false]
   166	    }
   167	
   168	    fn required_input_distribution(&self) -> Vec<Distribution> {
   169	        vec![self.dist_requirement.clone()]
   170	    }
   171	
   172	    fn maintains_input_order(&self) -> Vec<bool> {
   173	        vec![true]
   174	    }
   175	
   176	    fn children(&self) -> Vec<&Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   177	        vec![&self.input]
   178	    }
   179	
   180	    fn required_input_ordering(&self) -> Vec<Option<OrderingRequirements>> {
   181	        vec![self.order_requirement.clone()]
   182	    }
   183	
   184	    fn with_new_children(
   185	        self: Arc<Self>,
   186	        mut children: Vec<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>>,
   187	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   188	        Ok(Arc::new(Self::new(
   189	            children.remove(0), // has a single child
   190	            self.order_requirement.clone(),
   191	            self.dist_requirement.clone(),
   192	        )))
   193	    }
   194	
   195	    fn execute(
   196	        &self,
   197	        _partition: usize,
   198	        _context: Arc<TaskContext>,
   199	    ) -> Result<SendableRecordBatchStream> {
   200	        unreachable!();
   201	    }
   202	
   203	    fn statistics(&self) -> Result<Statistics> {
   204	        self.input.partition_statistics(None)
   205	    }
   206	
   207	    fn partition_statistics(&self, partition: Option<usize>) -> Result<Statistics> {
   208	        self.input.partition_statistics(partition)
   209	    }
   210	
   211	    fn try_swapping_with_projection(
   212	        &self,
   213	        projection: &ProjectionExec,
   214	    ) -> Result<Option<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>>> {
   215	        // If the projection does not narrow the schema, we should not try to push it down:
   216	        let proj_exprs = projection.expr();
   217	        if proj_exprs.len() >= projection.input().schema().fields().len() {
   218	            return Ok(None);
   219	        }
